| **i18n / translations** | `src/lib/i18n.js` + `i18n-zh.js`/`i18n-ja.js` + `scripts/i18n-extract.mjs` | t() wrapping rules + dictionary workflow in §16 — read it BEFORE adding UI strings |
| **CSS / visual styling** | `public/style.css` + `public/chat.css` + `public/viewers.css` | Split by component area |
| **HTML structure** | `public/index.html` | Sidebar, toolbar, workspace, dialogs |

### Architecture Patterns

- **All frontend cross-class communication** goes through `App` (mediator pattern). Classes receive `app` in constructor and call `app.methodName()`.
- **One-time WebSocket handler pattern**: Register via `ws.onGlobal()`, match on `type` + `sessionId`, remove self after first match. Used in `createSession()`, `attachSession()`, `resumeSession()`.
- **Debounced auto-save**: `LayoutManager.scheduleAutoSave()` waits 2s after last change. Blocked by `_restoring` flag for 5s on page load.
- **Resizer**: Reusable component with `inside: true` mode for fixed-position elements (sidebar). Don't set `position` or `flex` on elements that aren't flex children.
- **Layout restore**: `attachSession()` returns `winInfo` synchronously (the DOM element). Position is applied directly to this `winInfo`, NOT by guessing via `windows.values().pop()`. The WebSocket attach is async but the window element already exists.
- **Proportional bounds tracking**: `win.gridBounds` stores position `{left, top, width, height}` as fractions (0-1) of workspace. `_reflowWindows()` (via ResizeObserver) recalculates pixel positions on workspace resize. Applies universally — grid snap, edge snap, drag-drop, and `applyLayout()` all capture bounds. User resize updates proportions on mouseup. Works in both grid and freeform modes.
- **Overlap switcher**: Right-click on title bar detects overlapping windows via rect intersection (`_rectsOverlap`), shows popup at cursor position. Works in any mode — not tied to grid cells.
- **WebSocket reconnect re-attach**: On WS reconnect, all active sessions are re-attached. Chat sessions call `_reattach()` which re-sends attach → server responds with latest normalized messages + `isStreaming` from wrapper metadata. `globalHandlers` in ws.js are preserved across reconnects.
- **Layout sync (multi-client)**: State-based — full workspace state broadcast via `layout-sync` WS message after every change. Server saves + rebroadcasts (excluding sender). Receiver does smart diff via `_applyRemoteState()`: matches windows by unique ID, syncs positions/state/z-order, opens/closes windows as needed.
- **Atomic openSpec**: `createWindow({ openSpec })` sets the openSpec before `_notify()` fires, ensuring the first layout broadcast includes the window creation recipe. Only `createSession` (resume) sets openSpec async (in WS `created` callback) because serverId is unknown at creation time — it explicitly re-broadcasts via `scheduleAutoSave()`.
- **ChatView module split**: ChatView is the controller (virtual scroll, op dispatch). Rendering delegated to `ChatRenderers` (returns DOM elements). `renderSystemMsg` returns `{el, sideEffect}` to avoid circular deps — ChatView applies side effects to ChatStatusBar/ChatInput. Search, input, status bar, minimap are standalone classes receiving callbacks for cross-module communication.
- **Shared utilities**: `createPopover(anchor, className, opts)` handles popover positioning/dedup/close for all 7+ popover types. `showContextMenu(x, y, items)` is data-driven. `fetchJson(url)` wraps fetch+json+catch. `copyText(text)` with execCommand fallback.
- **Server-side settings reads use `serverSetting(key)`** (server.js; ws-handler gets it via deps) — backed by persistence.js's cached `readSettings` over data/settings.json, where /api/settings actually persists. `getSyncStore('settings')` is a dormant EMPTY migration-target store: 9 server reads through it silently returned defaults for every user-configured value until 2.87.0 (onDemandQuotaRefresh modes, activeUsagePolling, shipSubscriptionToRemote, per-turn reminder/stop nudge off-switches, telemetry toggles). Never read settings through the SyncStore server-side.
- **No native dialogs**: `prompt()/alert()/confirm()` are banned — use `showInputDialog`/`showConfirmDialog` (Promise-based, reuse `.dialog` CSS, Enter/Esc handled) and `showToast(msg, {type:'error'})` from utils.js. **Toasts are CARDS anchored at the inbox button (2.111.0)**: `configureToasts({getSeconds,getAnchor})` wired in app.js (duration = setting `taskbar.toastSeconds`; anchor falls back to the centered strip on mobile/hidden); every toast is recorded to localStorage history (`getToastHistory`) which the inbox popup shows as its Notifications tab (window CustomEvent `vs-toast` live-refreshes it). The pre-2.111.0 invisibility bug was `background: var(--bg-panel, var(--bg-secondary))` — BOTH undefined tokens → transparent (same class as the no-global-.hidden rule: verify computed styles, not class names). Storage-row gotcha: `.mounts-path` keeps its rtl left-truncation in an inner `.mounts-path-text` span — the type chip must stay OUTSIDE the rtl context or bidi reorders it to the end. Popovers/menus created via createPopover/showContextMenu carry `data-popover` so the global Escape handler (app.js `_setupDialogs`) closes them; Esc then closes `#dialog-overlay`. Esc is NOT intercepted while focus is inside `.xterm` (TUI apps need it).
- **Drag mousemove is rAF-coalesced everywhere** (window.js titlebar drag + resize, tab-group icon drag + tab drag-out): raw mousemove fires at pointer rate (125-1000Hz) and each `processMove` does elementFromPoint hit-tests (forced style recalc) + rect reads — uncoalesced this visibly stuttered with several live chat windows open. Pattern: store latest event, process once per `requestAnimationFrame`, cancel the pending frame in onUp. Keep new drag handlers on this pattern.
- **Cursor→window positioning MUST convert viewport→workspace coords (2.100.3, trace-diagnosed real report)**: `e.clientX/Y` are VIEWPORT coords; window `style.left/top` are WORKSPACE-relative (offset by sidebar ~260px + toolbar). Every "center on cursor" re-anchor that wrote raw clientX landed the window a sidebar-width away from the pointer (then tracked parallel — read as "drag drift"; invisible with the sidebar closed, which is why it survived across 7 sites: window.js un-snap/un-maximize/merge-ghost-leave/preview-leave + tab-group detach/follow/merge-leave). Convert via `workspace.getBoundingClientRect()`: `initL = (e.clientX - wsr.left) - w/2`. DELTA-based tracking (initL + (cx - startX)) is space-agnostic and safe — only absolute cursor placement needs the conversion. Also: after any mid-frame re-anchor of initL/startX, derive position from the CURRENT anchors at application time (a delta computed before the re-anchor is stale by the pointer's whole first-frame sweep under rAF coalescing). Diagnosis pattern that cracked it: temporary per-frame drag tracer shipped via `/api/telemetry` on mouseup — the user reproduces on THEIR machine, the agent reads the ndjson.
- **Sidebar session poll** (5s) pauses while `document.hidden` (30s heartbeat + immediate catch-up on visibilitychange) — single `_pollTimer` chain, never double-schedule.
- **Tab groups (chain model)**: Windows can be merged into tab groups by dragging one window's icon onto another. Shared chain object `{ tabs: [hostId, ...guestIds], active: index }` — all grouped windows hold the same reference via `win._tabChain`. `tabs[0]` is the host (owns the physical `.window` element). Guest content divs are reparented into the host element. Tab bar replaces title bar content with Chrome-style rounded tabs. Drag tab downward (>30px) to pull out — detached window raised to front via `focusWindow`, follows cursor with snap; entering another window's icon/tab bar collapses it to a `.tab-ghost` (same pattern as titleBar drag). Group resize/snap syncs all tabs' gridBounds via `_syncChainBounds`. Installed as a mixin on WindowManager from `tab-group.js`.
- **Tab merge hit-test**: Shared helper `_detectTabMergeTarget(x, y, sourceWinId, hiddenEls)` on tab-group mixin. Uses `elementFromPoint` after temporarily disabling `pointer-events` on the source and any ghost, so occluded icons never match. Used by (a) window.js titleBar drag, (b) `_setupIconDrag`, (c) `_setupTabDrag` after detach. All three share identical hit-test semantics.
- **Window type icons**: Each window type has an inline SVG icon (`TYPE_ICONS` in tab-group.js): terminal `>_`, chat bubble, files folder, viewer document, editor pencil, hex grid, browser globe. Shown in title bar, tab bar, taskbar, and overlap switcher. Icon is also the drag handle for tab merge. For chat/terminal windows with a backend, a composite icon is shown: backend logo (Claude/Codex) with a small mode badge (chat bubble / `>_` prompt) in the bottom-right corner. Taskbar icons use `transform:scale()` to uniformly enlarge the composite icon.
- **Move mode**: Right-click taskbar → Move. Full-screen overlay blocks all UI interaction. Window restores from maximized/snapped to original size. Click to place.
- **Loading screen**: Inline splash in HTML (no CSS dependency). Fades out after `app.ready` promise resolves (layout restore complete).

### Server-Side Key Functions

| Function | Location | Purpose |
|----------|----------|---------|
| `createEditorHelper()` | server.js | Generates `data/bin/code` script on startup |
| `attachToDtach()` | server.js | Creates PTY bridge to dtach socket |
| `restoreSessions()` | server.js | Reconnects to surviving dtach sessions on startup |
| `setupSessionPty()` | server.js | Wires PTY onData (chat JSON parser or terminal raw) + onExit |
| `refreshRateLimit()` | server.js | Non-billable `GET /api/oauth/usage` poll (read-only token, 429 backoff) |
| `registerWsHandler()` | src/ws-handler.js | All WebSocket message type handling (create/attach/kill/etc.) |
| `cwdToProjectDir()` | src/session-store.js | `cwd.replace(/[/._]/g, '-')` — deterministic encoding |
| `recoverCwdFromProjDir()` | src/session-store.js | Greedy reverse: try segments as-is, `.` prefix, `_` |
| `SessionMessages` | src/session-store.js | Unified JSONL+buffer access, chatStatus, taskState |
| `SyncStore` | src/sync-store.js | Versioned key-value store with diff broadcast |
| `broadcastActiveSessions()` | server.js | Pushes session list to all WebSocket clients |

## Key Design Decisions & Lessons Learned

### 1. dtach for Session Persistence (migrated from tmux)
**Decision**: Claude processes run in dtach sessions, NOT tmux or direct children of Node.js.

**Why dtach over tmux**: dtach is a minimal PTY detach/attach tool with ZERO rendering layer. tmux interposes its own terminal rendering that intercepts mouse events, scroll, escape sequences. After 6+ iterations of tmux mouse config (mouse on/off, send-keys -M, allow-passthrough, conditional bindings, stripping mouse sequences client-side), none worked correctly. dtach passes all PTY I/O transparently.

**Implementation**:
- Create: `dtach -c <socket> -E node pty-wrapper.js <buf> <meta> env EDITOR=... claude ...` (create+attach, with PTY wrapper for output buffering)
- Attach: `pty.spawn('dtach', ['-a', socketPath, '-E', '-r', 'winch'])` (SIGWINCH on attach)
- Server restart: scan `data/sockets/cw-*`, re-attach to surviving sessions, read buffer from wrapper's `.buf` file
- Metadata in `data/session-meta/<sockName>.json`
- Output buffer in `data/session-buffers/<sessionId>.buf` (written by pty-wrapper, survives server restart)

**PTY Wrapper** (`data/bin/pty-wrapper.js`): Runs inside dtach, uses node-pty to spawn claude. Tees all output to stdout (dtach PTY) + buffer file. Writes `childPid` to metadata file for server-side PID tracking (no pgrep needed). Survives server restarts — dtach keeps the wrapper alive, wrapper keeps writing the buffer. On server restart, `restoreSessions()` reads the buffer file to recover terminal content and the metadata file to recover PID mappings.

**Why dtach -c not dtach -n**: `dtach -n` creates a detached session — initial output is LOST because dtach doesn't buffer when no one is attached. `dtach -c` creates AND immediately attaches, so output flows through from the start.

**CRITICAL**: Never delete dtach socket files during server restart. The socket IS the session.

### 2. Mouse/Scroll Handling
With dtach, there is NO middle layer — xterm.js talks directly to Claude Code's PTY. Mouse events, scroll, selection all work natively without any configuration.

**Focus event filtering**: xterm.js sends `\e[I` (focus in) and `\e[O` (focus out) to the PTY when the terminal element gains/loses browser focus. In split-pane mode (Ctrl+G), clicking between the editor and terminal causes rapid focus/blur events → `^[[I^[[O` spam in the terminal. Fix: strip `\e[I` and `\e[O` from `terminal.onData()` before sending to PTY.

**Previous tmux failures** (for reference, do NOT retry):
1. ❌ `mouse off` + strip sequences → no scroll
2. ❌ `mouse off` + wheel→arrow keys → arrows = input history, not scroll
3. ❌ `mouse on` + `send-keys -M` → breaks selection
4. ❌ Strip `\e[?1000h` client-side → same as mouse off
5. ❌ `mouse on` + conditional binding → Claude doesn't set mouse_any_flag
6. ❌ `mouse on` + various unbind combos → selection still broken

### 3. Ctrl+G External Editor
**Problem**: Claude Code has a hardcoded GUI editor list: `["code","cursor","windsurf","codium"]`. If EDITOR matches, it does NOT clear the screen. Otherwise it calls `enterAlternateScreen()` (clears screen).

**Solution**: Create a fake `code` script at `data/bin/code`. Set `EDITOR=data/bin/code`. Script communicates via HTTP (POST `/api/editor/open`), not terminal I/O. Claude Code sees "code" → GUI editor → no screen clear → shows "Save and close editor to continue...".

**Flow**: Ctrl+G → Claude invokes `code -w <tmpfile>` → our script POSTs to server → server broadcasts `editor-open` via WebSocket → client splits terminal window (top=terminal, bottom=CodeMirror) → "Save & Close" button → writes file + creates signal file → script exits → Claude reads file. **AUTH (2.67.1):** the script's POST carries `Authorization: Bearer $VIBESPACE_SESSION_TOKEN`; auth.middleware exempts `/api/editor/open` and the ROUTE validates the vsst_ token against activeSessions — cookie-gating it (no exemption existed) silently broke Ctrl+G the moment password auth was enabled (script 401'd, claude hung on "Save and close editor to continue…").

**DO NOT**: Print anything to terminal from editor helper. DO NOT filter `\e[?1049h` sequences client-side (breaks TUI rendering). The `data/bin/code` script is regenerated by `createEditorHelper()` in server.js on every startup.

### 4. Session Discovery (redesigned 2026-03-24)
**Lock-first approach** — lock files are the source of truth for RUNNING, JONLs for HISTORY.

**Claude Code's internal session model:**
- Lock file: `~/.claude/sessions/<PID>.json` → `{pid, sessionId, cwd, startedAt}`
  - Created on start, deleted on graceful exit
  - `sessionId` changes on each `--resume` (new UUID, but JSONL filename stays original)
- JSONL file: `~/.claude/projects/<encodedCwd>/<originalSessionId>.jsonl`
  - Filename = original sessionId (immutable, even after multiple `--resume`)
  - Project dir encoding: `cwd.replace(/[/._]/g, '-')` (e.g. `/home/user/.config` → `-home-user--config`)

**Discovery algorithm:**
1. Scan lock files → filter alive PIDs → verify process is actually `claude` (avoids PID reuse)
2. Also scan tmux panes to determine if running claude is inside tmux (attachable)
3. For each alive lock, derive project dir from `lock.cwd` using the encoding formula
4. In that project dir, match locks to JSONLs via `claimJsonls` (session-store, PURE + unit-tested `scripts/test-claim-jsonls.mjs`; shared by local /api/sessions AND remote hosts.discoverSessions): **exact** (lock.sessionId or webui claudeSessionId = filename id) → **tail** (last 64KB scanned for `"sessionId":"<lock id>"` — a resumed session writes its CURRENT id into the ORIGINAL-named file; last-tail-id = current writer beats a mere mention) → **mtime fallback over NO-tail-evidence files only** (empty/unreadable — the brand-new-not-yet-flushed case; a file whose tail names some other dead id is a stopped session's transcript and is NEVER stolen; the leftover lock lists by its own sessionId instead). The pre-2026-07-11 "newest JSONL takes the lock" claim misattributed files whenever SEVERAL sessions ran in ONE cwd (real incident: 4 parallel external sessions read as 5 running; kill → WRONG id showed stopped → resume collided with a live session)
5. Each lock claims at most ONE JSONL; webui locks (known claudeSessionId) match exact-only; single-lock-single-jsonl dirs short-circuit with no tail read (the common case — full sweep stays well under the 4.5s cache TTL). Remote parity: the ssh discovery script emits `T <path>\t<tail ids>` lines (tail -c 65536 | grep, `2>/dev/null` — a host with broken tail degrades to the old mtime behavior)
6. All unclaimed JONLs → STOPPED
7. Status values: `tmux` (in tmux, attachable), `external` (unknown terminal, not attachable), `stopped`

**Why previous approaches failed:**
- ❌ Match lock to JSONL by sessionId ALONE: fails after `--resume` (new lock ID, old JSONL filename) — hence the tail pass
- ❌ Match by mtime alone: arbitrary attribution with N parallel sessions in one cwd (the 2026-07-11 lengyue incident) — mtime is now only the last-resort pass
- ❌ Match by cwd from inside JSONL: JSONL stores original cwd which may be stale after a directory move
- ❌ Match by cwd without dedup: one alive lock matches ALL JONLs in same directory (32 "running" for 10 PIDs)
- ❌ `recoverCwdFromProjDir()` greedy filesystem check: slow, fragile, wrong for moved directories

**Sidebar state machine:**
- **LIVE**: WebUI-managed (dtach), click to focus existing window
- **TMUX**: Running in external tmux, click to view (spawns `tmux attach -t <target>`). Closing window only detaches, does NOT kill the session.
- **EXTERNAL**: Running in unknown terminal, non-clickable
- **STOPPED**: Click to resume via `claude --resume`

### 5. Project Path Recovery
Claude encodes: `cwd.replace(/[/._]/g, '-')`. Forward direction (cwd → dir name) is deterministic.
Reverse direction (dir name → cwd) is ambiguous because `-` could be `/`, `.`, `_`, or literal `-`.
Recovery uses greedy filesystem checking as fallback, but the forward encoding is preferred.

### 6. Layout Persistence
- Auto-save: 500ms debounce after window changes, saves to `data/layouts.json`
- Restore: always uses autoSave on page load
- `_restoring` flag blocks auto-save for 1s during restore (prevents empty state overwriting)
- Captures `claudeSessionId` per terminal for cross-restart matching
- Grid state (`{rows, cols}`) persisted and restored — `setGrid()` triggers `_notify()` to save
- Custom grid presets stored in `layouts.json` → `customGrids` array, loaded on startup
- Window restore uses `winInfo` returned by `attachSession()` — NOT `windows.values().pop()` (see bug below)
- **All window types restored**: terminals (by claudeSessionId match), file explorers (by explorerPath), file viewers/editors (by filePath), browser windows (by URL)
- **Pre-snap size**: `preSnapBounds {width, height}` persisted per window, restored on layout load
- **Unique window IDs**: `win-{timestamp}-{random}` format for cross-client matching in layout sync
- **ID remap on layout restore**: taskbar buttons and other references use `winInfo.id` (not closure-captured id) to survive ID changes

### 6b. Layout Sync (Multi-Client)
- **State-based sync** (not op-based): full workspace state sent via WebSocket `layout-sync` after every change
- Server saves to disk (`data/layouts.json`) + broadcasts to all other clients (sender excluded via `ws !== senderWs`)
- **Receiver `_applyRemoteState`** does smart diff against local state:
  - Update positions, maximize/minimize state, snap state, z-order for matching windows (matched by unique `win.id`)
  - Open windows that exist in remote but not locally (creates sessions, file explorers, file viewers, browser windows)
  - Close windows that exist locally but not in remote state
  - File explorer navigation sync: calls `explorer.navigate()` on path change
- All coordinates use `gridBounds` (0-1 proportional), no pixel values in sync payload
- **Window creation sync via `openSpec`**: every window records `_openSpec` at creation — a serializable recipe to recreate it. **openSpec is UNCONDITIONAL, even on the syncId replay path (2.148.0)** — usage-window's `syncId ? undefined : spec` left every replayed copy transient on the receiving client (never re-synced onward, never closed by later diffs). Mutable per-window state that must survive refresh/sync lives IN the spec and is updated in place + scheduleAutoSave()d on change (browser: `url` AND `proxy` — proxy was a closure var, always reset to Off; the autosave call is safe inside navigate() because _userDirty/_restoring gate echoes). SAFEGUARD: captureState breadcrumbs `window-no-openspec:<type>` telemetry (deduped per type; TRANSIENT_WINDOW_TYPES = chat/terminal/stage-placeholder exempt) so a new window type added without a spec surfaces in Diagnostics instead of silently vanishing on other clients — the desktop/usage/browser bug class. `captureState` saves it, `_createRemoteWindow` replays via `app.replayOpenSpec(spec, syncId)`. Supported: `attachSession`, `openFileExplorer`, `openFile`, `openEditor`, `openBrowser`, `viewSession`, `viewSubagent`. Adding a new window type only requires setting `_openSpec` + one `replayOpenSpec` case.
- **Maximize/restore sync**: `toggleMaximize` and `restore` call `_captureGridBounds` after resize to capture correct proportional bounds
- 500ms autosave debounce ensures sync doesn't fire on every micro-change
- 1s `_restoring` cooldown prevents remote state application from triggering outbound sync
- **Anti-ping-pong protocol (2026-06-28 — do NOT regress any of these)**: an op on one client used to get undone and replayed several times. Four cooperating guards:
  1. **Seq**: server stamps every `layout-sync` rebroadcast with a monotonic `seq` (`layoutSyncSeqRef` in ws-handler); clients drop `seq <= _lastRemoteSeq` (stale echoes can't revert newer state). Counter resets with the WS connection (client resets `_lastRemoteSeq` on reconnect via `ws.onStateChange`).
  2. **User-dirty gate**: `_doAutoSave` only SENDS if a real local input (pointerdown/keydown, capture listeners) happened since the last remote apply (`_userDirty`, cleared at the end of `_applyRemoteState`, NOT cleared on send — so async user-initiated follow-ups like the resume openSpec re-broadcast still go out). **Dirty EXPIRES 60s after the last input (2.90.1)** — a stuck dirty bit on an idle client echoed stale positions with FRESH seq (the seq guard can't catch content-staleness), reverting other clients' drags; real incident from leftover automation tabs. This kills the echo: the capture/notify timers that fire after applying remote state escape the 1s cooldown but produce no send.
  3. **Defer-while-interacting**: inbound state while the pointer is down is stashed (`_pendingRemote`, latest wins) and applied 300ms after pointerup — remote broadcasts can't yank a window mid-drag.
  4. **Rounding convergence**: `_captureGridBounds` quantizes fractions to 4 decimals and the apply epsilon is 0.002 (integer `offsetLeft`px ÷ viewport gave apply→recapture drift ~0.0004 > the old 0.0001 epsilon → clients with different viewport sizes re-broadcast forever). Plus a no-op guard: identical serialized state is never re-sent (`_lastSentJson`).

### 6a. Grid Presets
- **Freeform button**: Clears grid, restores free-floating mode (`setGrid(null)`)
- **Built-in presets**: maximize (1×1), 2-col, 2-row, quad, 3-col — hardcoded in `applyLayout()`
- **Custom grid presets**: "+" button opens dialog, saves to server via `POST /api/custom-grids`, renders button with auto-generated SVG icon (≤4×4) or "RxC" text (>4×4). Right-click to delete.
- Custom grids use `grid-R-C` layout names (e.g. `grid-3-3`), parsed in `applyLayout()`
- `#custom-grids-container` uses `display: contents` to flatten into parent flex layout
- **All positioned windows track proportional bounds** via `win.gridBounds` `{left, top, width, height}` as fractions (0-1) of workspace. Captured after every positioning event: grid snap, edge snap, drag-drop, `applyLayout()`, user resize. `_reflowWindows()` (ResizeObserver on workspace) recalculates pixel positions on any workspace size change. Works in both grid and freeform modes.
- `gridBounds` is persisted in layout autoSave — on restore, positioned via `_applyGridBounds()` instead of absolute pixels, adapting to current workspace size
- **Timing**: `_captureGridBounds` must run AFTER snap animation completes (220ms). Use `setTimeout(..., 250)`, not `10`.

### 6c. Virtual Desktops
Each desktop is an independent layout slot with its own windows and grid mode. Windows are hidden via `visibility:hidden` + `pointer-events:none` (not `display:none`) — preserves scroll position, DOM state, and WebSocket handlers. Each browser tab independently tracks which desktop it's viewing (`_activeId` is local, not synced).

**Data model**: `layouts.json` has `desktopMeta: [{id, name}]` and `desktops: { [id]: { autoSave: {...} } }`. First load auto-migrates legacy `autoSave` to "Desktop 1". Every window gets `win._desktopId` tag at creation (intercepted `createWindow`). `captureState()` only serializes the active desktop's windows.

**Switching**: `switchTo()` hides current desktop windows, shows target desktop windows, applies target grid. **switchTo's merge-preserve (2.141.1, fast-switch protection) keeps openSpec-backed records absent from wm.windows — which is INDISTINGUISHABLE from "user closed it", so `wm.closeWindow` MUST call `desktopManager.purgeClosedWindow(id)` (2.152.0): without the purge every closed window resurrected on the next desktop round-trip as a lazy replay (real report; CDP repro in scripts/dbg-close-smoke.mjs). Any new dematerialize-a-window path needs the same decision: purge (user intent) or preserve (transient).** **Deleting the ACTIVE desktop runs the full switchTo pipeline (2.90.0)** — the old DOM-only show left a never-visited target desktop empty (its windows lazy-replay from _savedStates on first switch) and the closing autosave persisted that emptiness over the target's real layout; deleteDesktop is async now and waits out switchTo's re-entry guard. No re-rendering — `visibility:hidden` windows stay alive with full state (chat scroll, terminal content, etc.). Waiting blink (`window-waiting`) propagates to desktop preview rects in real-time.

**UI**: Ubuntu-style miniature previews in taskbar right corner. Each preview shows proportional window rectangles from `gridBounds`. Active desktop has accent border. Waiting windows blink yellow in preview. Click to switch, right-click for rename/delete, drag window onto preview to move it. "+" button to add desktop. Ctrl+Alt+Left/Right keyboard shortcut.

**Drag to desktop**: Window title bar drag detects desktop preview via `elementFromPoint` (temporarily `visibility:hidden` to see through). Entering a preview hides the window and creates a mini draggable rect inside the preview at cursor position. The source desktop preview's rect for this window disappears. Leaving restores the window. On drop, `gridBounds` is updated from mini rect position. On same-desktop drop, falls through to normal snap logic.

**Resizable taskbar**: Drag handle above taskbar (3px). Height 36-120px, persisted in localStorage + broadcast via `layout-sync`. All elements (desktop preview, taskbar icons, text, usage pies) scale proportionally via CSS variables set by `_adaptTaskbarSize()`. `_reflowWindows` suppressed during resize drag to prevent lag.

**WS protocol**: `layout-sync` extended with `desktopId` + `desktopMeta`. New: `desktop-create`, `desktop-delete`, `desktop-rename` → server persists + broadcasts `desktop-updated` (excluding sender). Remote clients update desktop list, reassign orphaned windows on delete.

**Tab groups**: `createTabChain`/`addToTabChain` enforce same desktop — guest inherits host's `_desktopId`. `applyLayout` filters by active desktop to prevent layout presets from affecting other desktops.

### 7. Modular Frontend (refactored 2026-03-23)
Split from monolithic 1647-line `src/client.js` into 13 ES modules under `src/lib/`. All cross-class communication goes through the `App` mediator. esbuild follows ES imports automatically, no build config changes needed.

### 7a. Mobile Architecture (refactored 2026-04-24)
Mobile-specific UI code extracted into dedicated modules to keep desktop and mobile rendering paths independent:
- **`src/lib/mobile-nav.js`** — `MobileNav` class: window switcher (tap title), close button (✕), desktop tabs, title updates, edge-swipe gestures; 2.99.0: ⚙ gear (gs-menu) + quota donut chip (usage popup) — see the file-structure entry. Only constructed when `app.isMobile` is true.
- **`src/lib/sidebar-render-mobile.js`** — `installSidebarRenderMobile` mixin: two-level folder/group navigation (folder list → drill-down → session cards). Architecturally different from desktop's collapsible groups.
- **`app.isMobile`** — centralized `matchMedia('max-width: 768px')` check in App constructor. All code references this instead of doing its own detection.
- **Mobile sidebar auto-yield is CENTRAL (2.99.2)**: `wm.createWindow` + `wm.focusWindow` call `_mobileYieldSidebar()` (window.js) — on mobile the sidebar is a full-screen overlay (z 90000), so any window open/focus with it open looked like a no-op (real report: card menu → Properties). Guarded by `layoutManager._restoring` ONLY (covers boot restore + remote layout-sync apply); deliberately NOT on `desktopManager._restoring` (stays true 1s past switchTo's resolve — would break cross-desktop Go-to-window, and no other switchTo path can run on mobile while the sidebar is open). `app._showDialog` also closes it (the index.html `#dialog-overlay` sits BELOW the sidebar; utils dialogs z 99998 + menus/popovers z 99999 render above it and need nothing). Do NOT add per-call-site `sidebar.toggle(false)` for windows/dialogs — it's centralized.
- **Mobile window-switcher is a chained-popover parent (2.99.2)**: its outside-tap close ignores taps inside `[data-popover]`/dialogs (same rule as attachPopoverClose) so the per-row billing chip's switcher menu + confirm keep the list open beneath them.
- **`app.isTouch`** — `matchMedia('(hover: none) and (pointer: coarse)')` — touch-primary device (phones AND tablets, independent of width). Gates touch affordances that aren't about layout.
- **Long-press = right-click** (`installLongPressContextMenu` in utils.js, installed when `app.isTouch`): 500ms still press synthesizes a bubbling `contextmenu` MouseEvent at the touch point, so ALL existing right-click menus (file explorer items/background/columns, sidebar group headers, mobile folder/group cards) work on touch with zero per-site code. iOS Safari never fires contextmenu natively; Android does — a trusted contextmenu cancels the pending timer (no double-fire). The post-long-press emulated click is suppressed via non-passive `touchend` preventDefault. Excluded surfaces: `textarea/input/select/[contenteditable]/.xterm` (native long-press behavior matters there).
- **Touch context menus**: `showContextMenu` submenus open on tap (click handler alongside mouseenter; open-only to avoid emulated-mouseenter double-toggle), clamp into viewport. `@media (hover: none)` enlarges menu rows to 40px touch targets.
- **Mobile terminal key row** (terminal.js `mobile-term-keys`, shown ≤768px): Esc/Tab/⇧Tab/sticky-Ctrl/arrows(hold-to-repeat 350ms→140ms)/📋 paste/^C ^G ^R ^Z ^D ^\. Sticky Ctrl transforms the NEXT typed letter to a control byte in `terminal.onData` (`_ctrlSticky`). 📋 = `_mobilePaste()`: async Clipboard API first (HTTPS; reads image blobs directly → `_uploadImageBlob` → /api/paste-image → `\x16` to PTY), falling back over HTTP to `_showPastePad()` — a visible contenteditable the user long-presses → Paste into, feeding the SAME paste-event pipeline as desktop Ctrl+V (image + bracketed text).
- **Chat links on touch**: tap shows an Open / Copy menu (`showContextMenu` at tap point) — there is no Ctrl key on touch, so the desktop click=copy / Ctrl+click=open split collapses into one menu. Right-click/long-press on links shows the same menu on all devices. iOS link callout suppressed via `-webkit-touch-callout: none`.
- **Code block Copy button**: in the code toolbar next to Wrap — strips line-number gutters (`.chat-code-text` join) and keeps diff +/- prefixes. Hover-revealed toolbars are always visible under `@media (hover: none)`.
- **Mobile sidebar cards**: long-press a group card → same context menu as desktop group-header right-click (rename/linked folders/delete); long-press a folder card → New session here / Copy path.
- **`_mobileDrilldown`** state on Sidebar: `{type: 'folder'|'group', key, label}` tracks drill-down position so `_render()` can restore it after session state changes (star/archive/resume) that trigger re-render.

### 8a. hljs multi-line spans × per-line split = code-block self-overlap (2.111.10, probe-diagnosed)
**The long-standing "code block lines paint overlapping themselves"**: `renderCodeBlock`/`rehighlightCodeBlock` split `hljs.highlight().value` by `\n` into per-line `<span class="chat-code-text">FRAGMENT</span>` rows — but hljs emits spans that CROSS newlines (markdown emphasis pairing `_` from `min_size`…`max_bytes` across lines, multi-line strings/comments). The naive split leaves an unclosed `<span>` on one line and a stray `</span>` on a later one; since ALL rows are joined into ONE innerHTML string, that stray close ends `.chat-code-text` EARLY and the rest of the line becomes extra ANONYMOUS FLEX ITEMS in the `.chat-code-line` flex row — `flex:1 + min-width:0` squeezes the real text span to near-zero (probe: 82 chars in 47.4px vs 353.2px siblings) and its `white-space:pre` content paints OVER the sibling items: overprint in nowrap, ~7-char narrow column in wrap. Layout row boxes stay perfectly stacked — paint corruption with clean layout geometry. Width-dependent squeeze ⇒ obvious on phones, subtle on wide desktops. Fix: `splitHighlightedLines()` (highlight.js) carries the open-span stack across fragments (append closes at line end, re-open at next line start) — used by BOTH render and rehighlight paths. Verify with the real pipeline + real content: minimal escHtml repros are structurally clean and prove nothing. Diagnosis pattern (2 wrong theories first — content-visibility 2.111.8, text-size-adjust 2.111.9, both probe-refuted): ship a geometry probe to the real device, then match its numbers byte-exact against a local structural test. Both refuted fixes kept as hygiene: `.chat-msg:has(.chat-code-block)` content-visibility carve-out (stale height cache is real for width-sensitive content) + `html { text-size-adjust: 100% }` (standard normalize boilerplate).

### 8b. 2026-07-12 交付夜 invariants (2.111.8–2.111.30 — details in CHANGELOG; do not regress)
- **Self-update is a UI dialog, not a terminal** (2.111.21/22): POST /api/self-update spawns update.sh DETACHED (log → data/update.log + `__UPDATE_EXIT:<code>` sentinel; survives the restart via systemd KillMode=process / the container supervisor); the dialog streams the log and reloads on the SERVER DOWN→UP TRANSITION or a version bump — never key the reload on version-change alone (re-running update on the latest restarts but the version stays equal; real report). update.sh resets generated tracked files (package-lock.json, data/bin/*) before `git pull --ff-only`. **2.112.7 — recurring "package-lock.json local changes would be overwritten" abort ROOT-FIXED**: the reset was a COMBINED `git checkout -- package-lock.json data/bin/vibespace-status`; on instances where `data/bin/vibespace-status` is UNTRACKED (it's generated + gitignored), the whole checkout aborts "pathspec did not match" and resets NEITHER, so package-lock.json stays dirty and the ff pull aborts. Now each path is reset INDEPENDENTLY (`git checkout HEAD -- package-lock.json` alone; tracked data/bin helpers per-path) + a stash-and-retry belt. An instance already stuck on an old update.sh needs a one-time manual `git checkout -- package-lock.json && git pull` to reach the fix (the buggy script can never self-heal past its own dirty lock).
- **Secret-scan CI (repo hygiene)**: `.github/workflows/secret-scan.yml` runs `scripts/secret-scan.mjs` (dependency-free; private keys / cloud+API tokens / DB URIs with passwords / high-entropy blobs — GENERIC rules only) on every push/PR. Org-specific denylists load from EXTERNAL files via `REPO_GUARD_COMPANY`/`REPO_GUARD_CREDS` (absent in CI → generic-only), so the scanner is safe to be public. Repo-level false positives go in `.repo-guard-allow`.
- **Version/update checks**: /api/version `latest` + /api/changelog-diff cache 15min; the gear menu + update dialog pass `?fresh=1` (60s floor). The old 6h cache showed "no update" for hours on release evenings.
- **Onboarding CLI login/install = embedded terminal modal** (runGuidedCli in setup-flows.js): ephemeral shell session rendered INSIDE a modal via a SYNTHETIC winInfo — TerminalSession only touches winInfo.{content,element,titleSpan,onResize}, so `{id, content: div, element: div, titleSpan: span}` suffices; polls /api/backend-status (file-existence, cheap) every 3s, ✓ + auto-close on completion; modal close kills the helper session. The wizard never disappears (modal z > wizard's 9600).
- **SSO (Clerk) skips passwords** (2.111.27): auth.ssoEnabled (clerk-only, distinct from .enabled) → app.locals → /api/home → app._ssoEnabled; onboarding step 2 shows "SSO configured, no password needed"; config-import disables the vsPassword row and the server pushes 'vsPassword: skipped (SSO configured)'.
- **/dav speaks DAV class 2 with ADVISORY (fake) locks** (2.111.16): macOS Finder mounts READ-ONLY unless the server advertises `DAV: 1, 2` and answers LOCK — fake lock tokens + accept-and-ignore PROPPATCH are the standard remedy (nginx dav_ext-style); ro tokens reject LOCK (403) so Finder shows them read-only. Basic auth accepted with the vsmt_ token as the password (Finder can't send Bearer); the share dialog surfaces dav URL + raw token + a paste-ready rclone.conf section.
- **Folder drag-drop onto the file explorer recurses via utils.collectDroppedFiles** (2.111.17): the flat dataTransfer.files list represents a dragged FOLDER as one unreadable pseudo-File (size 0) — uploads of it always fail. Entries are grabbed SYNCHRONOUSLY before the first await (they're neutered once the handler yields); readEntries loops (100-entry batches); files carry `_relPath`. Shared by chat drop + explorer.
- **Archive extraction runs as a polled server op** (2.111.18): streamed listing pass counts entries, verbose unzip/tar output bumps a live counter (extractOps map, GET/DELETE /api/archive/extract-status); the client renders it through the UPLOAD machinery (inline row + ring + popover + cancel). tar skip-existing tolerance regex is /(already |: File )exists/i — modern tar says "File exists".
- **Usage meters never vanish silently** (2.111.20): a CLI login with NO captured data renders gray "no data yet" donuts (chat sessions produce no passive statusline feed — fresh chat-only instances have an EMPTY usage-cache); only zero-login machines hide the meters.
- **VNC availability probe retries** (2.111.13/19): re-probe on ws reconnect + failure backoff 3s→90s×5 — a page loaded during a restart window must self-heal the Desktop entry. fetchJson returns null on HTTP failure (retry) vs a real available:false (terminal).
- **Mountpoint hygiene** (2.111.21): user unmount / customPath change / remove sweep the leftover dir via rmdir ONLY (non-empty stays), 1.5s delayed past lazy-unmount.

### 8. xterm.js Rendering Gotchas
- **WebGL renderer (2026-07-02)**: terminals load `@xterm/addon-webgl` (fallback to the DOM renderer on failure/context-loss, `onContextLoss` → dispose). The DOM renderer laid rows out with browser-rounded letter-spacing while FitAddon computed cols from the UNROUNDED cell width — the accumulated fraction CLIPPED THE RIGHTMOST COLUMN. WebGL uses device-pixel-aligned integer cell metrics (verified 8×21px) — do not remove it "for simplicity". The terminal container is painted in the terminal theme's background (`_syncContainerBg`, applied on theme change + per-terminal override) so the up-to-one-cell layout remainder is invisible instead of reading as "the TUI is smaller than the window". A devicePixelRatio watcher (matchMedia resolution, re-armed per change) clears the texture atlas + refits on zoom/monitor change.
- **Multi-client attach/cap (2026-07-02)**: on a client's FIRST real fit after attach, if `resizeSessionToMin` leaves the PTY size unchanged the server nudges it one column down and back (dtach `-r winch` trick) — without this the TUI got no SIGWINCH and the fresh client stayed on a partial buffer replay (garbled after refresh). When a smaller client is the binding constraint, `effective-size` carries `clients` (real terminal count) and `_updateCapIndicator` renders THREE states: CAPPED (smaller client bounds the PTY) → hatched unused region + badge + "Use my size" takeover button; BLOCKED (a larger client took over and the PTY exceeds this window) → full overlay + "Resume here" (takes ownership back); OWNER (own override active) → "Size override active" badge + Release. Protocol: `size-override` {sessionId, release?} sets `session._sizeOwnerWs`; `resizeSessionToMin` sizes the PTY to the owner's live size instead of the min and broadcasts `override:true`; ownership evaporates when the owner's clients-map entry disappears (disconnect). A blocked client does NOT resize its local xterm up (would overflow the container) — content garbles behind the overlay, repainted via SIGWINCH on the next ownership change. Badge only when clients>1 — a solo mismatch is just a resize in flight.
- **Terminal query-response arbitration (2.101.0, real report)**: an app's terminal query (OSC 11 bg color, `\e[6n` CPR, DA…) is answered by EVERY attached client (dtach has no middle emulator) — the app consumes one answer, the tty ECHOES the extras as literal `^[]11;rgb:…^[[3;1R` junk; buffer REPLAY re-answers stored queries the same way. Fixes (keep BOTH): ws-handler `input` forwards pure query-response chunks only from ONE designated client (size owner, else oldest) when >1 attached (TERM_QUERY_RESP_RE — kept in sync with terminal.js; accepted collision: modified-F3 `\e[1;2R` from a non-owner client is eaten); client-side, `term._replaying` (set around the session-lifecycle buffer-restore write) makes terminal.js onData drop xterm's auto-answers during replay.
- **Alternate-screen awareness**: the pin-to-bottom freeze machinery (wheel unpin + output queueing) only applies on the NORMAL buffer. On the alternate screen (claude's fullscreen renderer, vim, htop) the TUI owns the viewport — frames write through immediately (queued output is flushed on the way in) and wheel events are left to mouse reporting.
- **Claude fullscreen TUI (CLI ≥2.1.x)**: `/tui fullscreen` ⇄ `/tui default` (persisted in CLI prefs); env `CLAUDE_CODE_NO_FLICKER=1` forces the flicker-free alt-screen renderer with virtualized scrollback, `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_ALTERNATE_SCREEN=1` forces classic. WebUI setting `claude.tuiRenderer` (Auto/Fullscreen/Classic) → client passes `tuiRenderer` in the create message (terminal mode only) → `ClaudeCodeAdapter.buildSessionArgs` returns it in `sessionSpec.env` → ws-handler injects via the `env` command in the dtach spawn line. Verified end-to-end (env in /proc + one `\x1b[?1049h` alt-enter in the buffer).
- **Web fonts are SELF-HOSTED since 2.137.0** (public/fonts/*.woff2 + /fonts.css, OFL): fonts.googleapis.com is BLOCKED for users behind national firewalls — hosted CSS never arrived, first terminal stayed on the canvas fallback forever, and no client-side polling can heal an unreachable origin (recurring onboarding reports). Never reintroduce a third-party font origin. The registration-polling machinery below stays as the residual same-origin race healer.
- **Web-font FOUT needs REGISTRATION polling (2.105.0, real cold-cache report)**: before the Google Fonts CSS itself loads, every fonts API lies — `load()` resolves empty, `fonts.ready` resolves early, and `check()` returns TRUE for an UNREGISTERED family (only a registered-but-unloaded face gives false). `_refreshOnFontReady` polls `document.fonts` for the family to APPEAR (500ms×40), then load()s and clearTextureAtlas()+refits when faces deliver. Do not "simplify" back to load/ready/check.
- **Font change requires `clearTextureAtlas()`**: xterm.js canvas/WebGL renderer caches font glyphs in a texture atlas. Setting `terminal.options.fontFamily` alone does NOT re-render — must call `terminal.clearTextureAtlas()` after changing font family or font size for the change to take visual effect, then call `fit()` to recalculate dimensions.
- **Focus events**: When focus reporting is enabled (`\e[?1004h`), xterm.js sends `\e[I`/`\e[O` on focus/blur. These must be filtered from `onData()` to prevent `^[[I^[[O` spam in split-pane UI.
- **Cursor**: Set `cursorBlink: false, cursorStyle: 'bar', cursorInactiveStyle: 'none'` — Claude Code TUI renders its own visual cursor, so xterm.js's hardware cursor should be minimized.
- **Pin-to-bottom / scroll freeze**: When user scrolls up (detected via `wheel` event, not xterm `onScroll` which fires on programmatic scrolls too), output is queued in `_pendingOutput` instead of written to terminal. Terminal freezes in place. When user scrolls back to bottom or clicks the ↓ button, `_repin()` writes all queued output and scrolls to bottom. This prevents Claude Code's TUI redraw (`\e[H` cursor home) from yanking the viewport.
- **Idle detection via OSC 0**: Claude Code updates terminal title via `\e]0;...\a`. First character indicates state: `✳` (U+2733) = idle/waiting for input, braille chars (U+2800-28FF) = working. Detected via `terminal.parser.registerOscHandler(0, ...)`. When transitioning to idle while window not focused, `window-waiting` class triggers orange blink animation on title bar + taskbar item. Cleared on focus.

### 9. Usage / Rate Limit Monitoring (non-invasive, since 2026-06-22)
**Approach**: `GET /api/oauth/usage` every ~5 min (`_fetchOAuthUsage`). Non-billable — returns 5h/7d utilization + resets directly in the body (`five_hour`/`seven_day`: `{utilization (0–100 %), resets_at (ISO)}` → mapped to our `{utilization (0–1), resetsAt (unix s)}`). Endpoint rate-limits HARD on bursts (~5 rapid reqs → 429, retry-after 300s; verified), so: one request per interval, `_rateLimitBackoffUntil` honors the 429 retry-after, keep last-known on any failure, jittered first poll. Frontend already shows "Updated Xmin ago" from `fetchedAt` (only bumped on a 200) → staleness is visible.

**READ-ONLY OAuth token (issue #20)**: `getOAuthToken()` NEVER refreshes the token — it returns the stored access token only if currently valid (60s skew), else null (caller skips, keeps last-known; Claude Code refreshes it via its own session activity and the next poll picks it up). The old auto-refresh was invasive: Anthropic's refresh tokens **rotate**, so our 5-min poll burned the refresh token Claude Code still had stored — on macOS (Keychain, which we can't safely rewrite) this forced a daily re-login. There is no `_refreshOAuthToken`/`_saveRefreshedToken` anymore; we never write tokens anywhere. `_readOAuthCreds` reads `.credentials.json` (Linux) / Keychain (macOS) read-only, mtime-cached.

**Available data**: 5-hour utilization, 7-day utilization, reset timestamps, status (allowed/limited). Model-scoped weekly caps (e.g. Fable) ride in `limits[]` as `kind:'weekly_scoped'` with `scope.model.display_name` — parsed into `scopedWeekly: [{name, utilization, resetsAt, severity}]` and shown as their own bar in the usage popup. Taskbar pies are donuts with 5h/7d labels in the hole. Spend/extra-usage not yet surfaced.

**Model discovery**: `refreshAvailableModels()` — `GET /v1/models` for BOTH auth types (OAuth: Bearer + `anthropic-beta: oauth-2025-04-20`; API key: `x-api-key`). Runs 3s after startup then hourly. Full model IDs come from the API; CLI aliases (`fable`/`opus`/`sonnet`/`haiku` + `[1m]` variants) are hardcoded in `CLAUDE_MODEL_ALIASES` since they're CLI-side names — when a new tier ships, add its alias there (+ fallbacks in `app.js` BACKEND_SESSION_OPTIONS and `settings-schema.js` claude.defaultModel). History: `/api/claude_cli/bootstrap`'s `additional_model_options` was the OAuth source until ~2026-06 when it started returning null; `/v1/models` used to 401 for OAuth tokens but now accepts Bearer.

**OAuth auth headers (2026-06)**: OAuth tokens must use `Authorization: Bearer` + `anthropic-beta: oauth-2025-04-20` on api.anthropic.com — sending an OAuth token via `x-api-key` returns 401 "invalid x-api-key" (this silently froze the usage poll until fixed). Real API keys (`sk-ant-api…`) still use `x-api-key`.

**Failed approaches:**
- ❌ Parse statusline output: user-customizable, can't guarantee format
- ❌ Statusline hook wrapper (`--settings`): intrusive, doesn't work for non-WebUI sessions
- ❌ macOS `security unlock-keychain`: works but requires empty keychain password, invasive
- ❌ Billable haiku `/v1/messages` + response headers: worked, but consumed quota to measure quota AND needed a fresh token → drove the token refresh that rotates + breaks the macOS Keychain (#20). Superseded 2026-06-22.
- ❌ Self-refreshing the OAuth token (`platform.claude.com/v1/oauth/token`): rotates Anthropic's refresh token out from under Claude Code → forced re-login on macOS. Removed.
- ✅ `GET /api/oauth/usage` (non-billable) + read-only token + 429 backoff: current approach. Earlier rejected for "aggressive rate limiting" — but that was *burst* polling; one request per ~5 min sustains fine (verified: 14/14 over 30 min at 2-min cadence, zero token rotation).
- ✅ `/v1/models` with OAuth Bearer: model discovery source (both auth types), now also read-only token.

### 10. Settings System (Global + Per-Terminal)
**Global settings** (toolbar ⚙): Theme, font size (A-/A+), font family. Stored in `localStorage` (`termFontSize`, `termFontFamily`). Changes propagate to all terminals without per-terminal overrides.

**Per-terminal settings** (window titlebar ⚙): Same three options, each with a "Default" that follows global. Theme and font have Default as a dropdown option. Font size has a Default checkbox that disables the number input. Overrides stored in `TerminalSession.overrides` and persisted in layout.

**Schema-driven settings** (`settings-schema.js`): VS Code-style settings UI. Opens as a NON-BLOCKING same-level window (2.53.0 — `SettingsUI.open()` calls `wm.createWindow({type:'settings'})`, singleton-focus, no openSpec so it's transient; the old `.settings-overlay` modal is gone) so a setting can be tweaked while the workspace effect is visible. `.settings-dialog.settings-window` fills the window content. Categories: Toolbar & Layout, Window, Terminal, Sidebar, Session Card, Chat, Session. **Rule: only add settings that have working code behind them** — no placeholder/aspirational entries. Settings with `liveApply: false` need explicit one-shot listeners if they must be applied after async load (see `defaultStatusFilter` pattern). File explorer sort/filter config uses its own localStorage persistence — these are operational state, not user settings. Notable settings: `chat.roleIndicator` (border/background/icon/label), `session.defaultMode` (terminal/chat, default: chat), `chat.uploadDir` (2.148.0 — where chat drag-drop/attach uploads land: empty = session cwd; absolute /…|~/… verbatim (server expandTilde's LOCAL dests; remote sessions resolve on the remote); bare name = subfolder under cwd; drop-overlay hint reflects it). `chat.hideEmptyThinking` (default ON, 2.108.1): empty thinking cards (redacted/zero-length — REAL thinking is structurally never adjacent; the adjacent pairs are these stubs) hide via body class `hide-empty-thinking`; hidden cards are TRANSPARENT to run-collapse (`_updateRuns` kind 'skip': neither count nor break adjacency — an invisible stub between two Bash cards used to silently split the run).

**Session card click behavior**: `sessionCard.clickBehavior` enum: `focus` (default — click opens/focuses window), `expand` (click toggles card details), `flash` (click flashes/bounces the window), `goto` (switch desktop + flash). Expand/collapse is always available via the ▸ arrow button regardless of this setting.

**Find/GoTo split button**: Session card detail panel has a Find/GoTo split button (like Resume). Find flashes window + taskbar + desktop preview rect. GoTo switches to the window's desktop and flashes. Mode persisted via `sessionCard.findMode` setting (broadcast to all clients). For tab group guests, both resolve to the host window and switch to the target tab first.

### 11. Chat Mode (Dual-Mode Architecture)
**Two session modes** share the same dtach persistence layer but use different wrappers:
- **Terminal**: `dtach → pty-wrapper.js → claude` (TUI, raw PTY output, xterm.js)
- **Chat**: `dtach → chat-wrapper.js → claude --output-format stream-json --input-format stream-json --verbose --permission-prompt-tool stdio` (structured JSON, ChatView)

**chat-wrapper.js**: Runs inside dtach, spawns claude with stream-json flags + `--permission-prompt-tool stdio`. Parses stdout JSON lines, writes to buffer file. Stdin: accepts JSON messages (JSONL schema: `{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"..."}]}}`). Plain text on stdin auto-wrapped. Also handles `control_request`/`control_response` protocol for permission approval over stdin/stdout.

**Permission Approval**: Uses `--permission-prompt-tool stdio` flag (undocumented, discovered from HAQI). Claude sends `control_request` on stdout, server handles `permission-response` WS message → writes `control_response` to stdin with `updatedInput`. Permission UI embedded inline in tool cards (not separate messages): pending shows Allow/Always Allow/Deny buttons between Input and Output; resolved shows collapsed ✓ Allowed/✗ Denied. "Always Allow" passes `permission_suggestions` back as `permission_updates` for session-wide rules. On attach, server separates `control_request` from buffer into `pendingPermissions` map, filters resolved ones, sends in attach payload. Client injects after tool cards render. Permission mode shown in status bar (🔒 default/bypassPermissions/etc.).

**ChatView** (`src/lib/chat-view.js`): Controller consuming normalized `msg` ops (create/edit/meta) from MessageManager. Virtual scroll, op dispatch (`_onOp` → `_onCreateMessage`/`_onEditMessage`/`_onMeta`), lifecycle. Delegates rendering to `ChatRenderers`, input to `ChatInput`, status to `ChatStatusBar`, search to `ChatSearch`, minimap to `ChatMinimap`. Each message has a stable ID → one DOM element tracked via `_elements` Map. Edit ops re-render in place (no append-and-match). No `_pendingToolUses` — tool state managed by MessageManager.

**ChatRenderers** (`src/lib/chat-renderers.js`): All message rendering — `renderUserMsg`, `renderAssistantMsg`, `renderToolMsg`, `renderToolResult`, `renderSystemMsg`, `renderPermissionOverlay`, `renderEditDiff`, `renderMarkdown`. Linkification via unified `linkifySegment` (URL + path regex). Wrap toggles + searchable language picker. `renderSystemMsg` returns `{el, sideEffect}` so ChatView applies model/permMode/slashCommands without circular deps.

**ChatInput** (`src/lib/chat-input.js`): Textarea, send, attachments, slash command dropdown, draft persistence, streaming status indicator, TODO display, interrupt button. **File/folder upload**: a paperclip button (mobile/click entry point) → Files/Folder menu; `uploadFiles()` POSTs to `/api/upload` with `destDir` = the session cwd (`getCwd` callback) + `fileNames` + `preservePaths` (inferred from relative paths). `_insertUploadedPaths` inserts one shell-quoted path per top-level item at the cursor. Desktop also drag-drops onto the whole chat view: `ChatView._setupChatDrop` (editable views only) shows a dashed overlay and `_collectDroppedFiles` recurses dropped directories via the DataTransfer entries API. Backend-agnostic.

**ChatStatusBar** (`src/lib/chat-status-bar.js`): Model badge, context %, cache ratio, cost, permission mode dropdown, background task popup.

**Tool call rendering**: Tool calls are normalized as `role:'tool'` messages. Pending: `status:'pending'` with `tool_call` content block (spinner). Complete: server sends edit op → `status:'complete'` with `tool_result` content block → ChatView re-renders via `_onEditMessage`. Interrupted: `tool_call` with error status shows `✗ Interrupted` indicator. Agent tools include View Log button. Clickable paths/URLs via unified `linkifySegment` (HTML-aware, linkifies inside `<code>` blocks). No output truncation.

**Subagent/Agent rendering**: Subagent messages (`parent_tool_use_id` or `isSidechain`) filtered from main chat. Server buffers by `parentToolUseId` in `session.subagentBuffers`, broadcasts as both `subagent-message` (for parent tool card status) and normalized `msg` ops with virtual session ID `sub-{toolUseId}` (for subagent viewer via per-subagent normalizers `_subNormalizers` Map). "View Log" button opens read-only ChatView (`readOnly: true` — no input area, no status bar, normal scroll with pin-to-bottom) attached to a virtual session. Duplicate viewers prevented: `_subagentViewers` Map tracks open windows by virtualId, clicking View Log again focuses existing window. Live agents use `sub-{parentToolUseId}` virtual sessions — server returns buffered messages on attach and forwards new ones. Completed agents use `sub-agent-{agentId}` — server loads from `subagents/agent-{agentId}.jsonl`. No client-side `_subagentBuffers`/`_subagentViews` — all buffering/forwarding handled server-side via virtual session attach.

**Workflow detail viewer (dynamic-workflow / ultracode; LIVE while running + full snapshot when done, 2.36.1; REMOTE sessions since 2.191.0 — `?host=` on /api/workflow + host in the openWorkflowDetail openSpec/status-chip poll/stage probe, server pulls snapshot+journal via hosts.fetchWorkflowState and agent transcripts via fetchAgentJsonl for the `sub-agent-` attach's hostId)**: while a run is IN PROGRESS `/api/workflow` returns a live skeleton from `journal.jsonl` (agent count + per-agent running/done) — `workflow-detail.js` renders a pulsing "Running" chip + "N agents · M done · running…" + a row per agent with a live transcript (View Log), and POLLS every ~2.5s until the terminal snapshot replaces it, then auto-switches to the full phase/label/token view. Running view has NO phase names/labels/tokens (those exist only in the end-of-run snapshot). RESUME staleness guard (2.185.0, real report): resumeFromRunId REUSES the runId, so a killed run's terminal snapshot shadowed the whole resumed execution — /api/workflow serves the LIVE skeleton (+`resumed:true` → 'resumed after an interruption' tag) when the run dir's journal/agent mtimes exceed the snapshot's by >15s (completed runs write the snapshot ≤0.1s after the last journal line), and the client keeps a SLOW 15s re-poll on killed/failed runs (an open viewer used to stopPoll() forever on a terminal state). Retry chains (2.181.1): journalAttempts derives superseded attempts (same journal key, non-newest started, no result — the harness re-spawned an aborted agent) and both live view + snapshot tag them state 'superseded' → chip 'retried — replaced by a newer attempt' (their logs dead-end in the CLI's canned '[Request interrupted by user]', which read as phantom user interrupts; real report). The rest (the post-hoc snapshot path): a `Workflow` tool card (Claude's dynamic-workflow orchestrator) renders a **View Workflow** button (`chat-renderers.js` parses the runId from the launch ack `Run ID: wf_…` / `resumeFromRunId`). It opens window type `workflow` (`workflow-detail.js` → `app.openWorkflowDetail(runId,{claudeSessionId,cwd,name})`, openSpec `openWorkflowDetail`) that fetches `/api/workflow` and renders phases → agents (state chip queued/progress/done/error + model) + run token/tool totals + Result/Error. Each agent's **View Log** reuses the EXISTING subagent viewer via a `viewSubagent` openSpec (`sub-agent-<agentId>`) — the server's subagent lookup was extended to also search `subagents/workflows/wf_*/agent-<id>.jsonl`, so zero new viewer code. FILE-FORMAT REALITY (verified empirically + vs third-party claude-view): a workflow writes THREE artifacts under `<projDir>/<claudeSessionId>/` — (1) `workflows/wf_<runId>.json` = the RICH snapshot (phases + `workflowProgress[{type:workflow_phase|workflow_agent, phaseIndex, label, model, state, agentId}]` + totals), written by the CLI's `pel()` **ONCE at terminal state** (completion/kill/fail), NOT live (a 28s probe's file appeared only at the end; killed runs freeze mid-run states); (2) `subagents/workflows/wf_<runId>/journal.jsonl` = the resume cache (`{started|result, key, agentId}`, live-appended, NO phase/label); (3) `subagents/workflows/wf_<runId>/agent-<id>.jsonl` = per-agent transcripts (identical schema to a normal subagent JSONL, stream live). The parent stream-json only carries the `Workflow` tool_use (the script) + an `async_launched` tool_result `{runId, workflowName, transcriptDir}` + a background-completion notification + `turn_duration.pendingWorkflowCount` — NO per-phase/agent progress. So a LIVE progress tree has no clean source (phase/label mapping exists only in the terminal snapshot); the viewer is intentionally post-hoc (killed/failed runs still open, showing frozen states). See [[claude-code-internals-analysis]] "Dynamic workflows".

**JSONL file watcher workaround**: stream-json does not emit subagent assistant text messages (known bug: anthropics/claude-code#8262). Server works around this by watching subagent JSONL files via `fs.watch()`. On `system.task_started`, `startSubagentWatcher()` opens the JSONL file and reads new lines on each change event. Messages are deduplicated by uuid against those already emitted via stream-json (tracked in `session.subagentEmittedUuids`). On `system.task_notification`, the watcher is stopped. This provides complete subagent message coverage despite the stream-json gap.

**Interrupt**: Inline "■ Stop" button in streaming status bar (only visible while Claude outputs). Delayed-fallback pattern: sends `control_request` with `subtype: 'interrupt'` to claude stdin immediately, then schedules SIGINT 2 seconds later. Before firing SIGINT, `postInterrupt` re-reads the wrapper meta file — if `streaming:false` the protocol interrupt worked and SIGINT is skipped (avoids killing the whole session in newer Claude Code versions that exit on SIGINT). Sending a new chat message during the 2s window also cancels the pending SIGINT. Historical context: bugs anthropics/claude-code#17466 and #3455 — the SIGINT fallback was originally added because the protocol interrupt was unreliable.

**Background task tracking**: Two sources of background tasks: `system.task_started` (Agent tool) and `tool_use.run_in_background` (Bash/commands). Tracked in `_activeTasks` Map keyed by tool_use_id. Status bar shows count. Click opens popup with task details — agent tasks open View Log (subagent viewer), command tasks open editor with input+output. `task_progress` updates description/lastTool. `task_notification` removes completed tasks.

**TODO display**: Positioned above streaming status, above input area. Populated from `TodoWrite` tool_use input (Claude) and `turn/plan/updated` notifications (Codex plan tool — wrapper emits `plan_updated` event_msg, normalizer maps `{step,status}` → TodoWrite shape, persisted in wrapper `meta.plan` for attach restore via `taskState().todos`). Shows current `in_progress` item with hourglass icon and progress count (completed/total). Click expands full todo list popup with all items and their status icons (completed/in_progress/pending). Hidden when all items completed.

**Model dropdown (mid-session switch)**: the status-bar model badge is clickable → dropdown from `/api/available-models` (+ Custom… input). `set-model` WS → adapter `formatSetModel`: Claude writes control_request `{subtype:'set_model', model}` (CLI ≥2.1.x; verified live) — the CLI echoes `<local-command-stdout>Set model to X (resolved-full-id)` as a user record, which ChatView parses to set the badge to the RESOLVED id (the control_response says success even for bogus names, so the echo is the only authoritative confirmation); Codex writes wrapper `{type:'set-model'}` → `meta.model`, applied on the next `turn/start` (model is a per-turn param), confirmed by turn_context. HONEST DISPLAY RULES (do not regress): the badge always renders — CLI-reported value or an explicit `model: ?`; never strip `[1m]`; never default contextWindow to 200k (only the used>190k ⇒ 1M deduction is sound) — unknown window renders `used/?` with no percentage.

**Effort dropdown (mid-session switch)**: separate clickable badge next to the model. Claude: NO set_effort subtype exists and `/effort` is BLOCKED in stream-json (non-interactive command blocklist) — the working mechanism is control_request `apply_flag_settings` with settings key **`effortLevel`** (NOT `effort` — wrong keys are silently swallowed; the response is success-blind even for garbage). This is the CLI's own path (its /effort command sends exactly this on remote transports). Verified live: same question at max vs low = 3306 vs 353 thinking chars; overrides a spawn-time `--effort` flag; `effortLevel:null` resets. Claude NEVER reports effort back (no echo, no JSONL field) → the badge shows the last COMMANDED value (spawn `--effort` via `session._effort` merged into chatStatus at attach, mirroring `_permissionMode`; updated by `set-effort`), tooltip says "as last commanded". Codex: wrapper `{type:'set-effort'}` updates the mutable `effort` var → next `turn/start` (per-turn param), confirmed by turn_context. Effort levels for the dropdown come from `/api/session-options` (parsed from `claude --help` — a wrapped `(low, medium, high, xhigh, max)` line; that IS the effortLevel enum). **`ultracode` is NOT an effortLevel** — it's a separate boolean settings key (= xhigh + standing dynamic-workflow orchestration), appended as a client-side pseudo-level (mirrors the CLI's /effort UI); `formatSetEffort` sends `{effortLevel:'xhigh', ultracode:true}` for it (from disassembling /effort — the CLI sends BOTH keys), `{effortLevel:X, ultracode:false}` otherwise; spawn ultracode → `--effort xhigh --settings '{"ultracode":true}'`. Gated CLI-side on an xhigh-capable model + dynamic workflows. A brand-new ChatView renders the status bar immediately (`model: ?` / `effort: ?`) instead of an empty bar.

**Model auto-fallback warning (2.29.1)**: the CLI silently swaps models under load, writing a `{type:'fallback', from:{model}, to:{model}}` content block in the assistant record while `message.model` flips (verified from a 279MB real session: 61 transitions, zero manual switches). The claude normalizer emits a `served-model` meta whenever the serving model changes + a system notice on the fallback block; `ChatStatusBar.setServedModel` + `_modelMismatch` (alias-tolerant: strip `claude-` prefix + `[1m]`, core startsWith both ways — 'fable' vs 'claude-fable-5' is NOT a mismatch) turn the model badge amber with ⚠ + the actual serving model; clears when the requested model serves again. Mid-session model/effort picks from the status bar also persist as that session's per-session config via `ChatView._persistSessionConfig` (statusBar `onConfigChange` → sidebar.setSessionConfig keyed by the live session match or openSpec.backendSessionId).

**Permission mode dropdown**: Click the lock icon in status bar to open dropdown with available permission modes (fetched from `claude --help` output). Selecting a mode sends `set-permission-mode` WebSocket message → server writes `control_request` with `subtype: 'set_permission_mode'` to claude stdin. Mode badge always shown in status bar (defaults to 'default' if unknown).

**AskUserQuestion UI**: `AskUserQuestion` arrives via `control_request` (`tool_name === 'AskUserQuestion'`, same channel as permissions). Normalizer marks the tool message `permission.kind = 'user_input'` with `questions`. ChatRenderers renders a paginated questionnaire — one question per page with ← → nav + page indicator, selectable option cards (single-select highlights, multi-select toggles), a custom-answer text input per question (mutually exclusive with option selection), and a Submit button enabled only when every question is answered. Response: `permission-response` with `approved: true` + `toolInput: { ...origInput, answers: { "<question text>": "<selection>" } }` (NOT the old `responseData` shape).

**/goal command** (chat mode, both backends): session-scoped objective the agent auto-continues toward. Chat input intercepts `/goal <text>` → `set-goal` WS message (`/goal` shows status, `/goal clear` clears, `/goal resume` re-activates `_prevGoal`). Server forwards to wrapper + broadcasts `goal-updated`. Goal state (`_goal`, `_goalStatus`, `_goalElapsed`, `_goalTokensUsed`, `_prevGoal`) lives on the session, persisted in wrapper meta, read in `restoreSessions`, sent in attach response.
- **Claude**: NATIVE since CLI ~2.1.1xx (`/goal` gained `supportsNonInteractive: true` — dispatched as a command in stream-json, verified live on 2.1.170; older CLIs echo it as plain text). Wrapper's `set-goal` handler forwards `/goal <text>` / `/goal clear` as a stream-json user message — setting a goal immediately starts a model turn, then the CLI's Stop hook drives continuation AND met-detection (no wrapper simulation, no iteration cap). CRITICAL GAP: `goal_status` attachments (`{condition, met, reason, iterations, durationMs, tokens, sentinel}`) are **JSONL-only** — NOT emitted on stream-json stdout (same class as subagent gap #8262). Server syncs via `checkClaudeGoalStatus()`: after each `result` with an active goal, tail-read (64KB) the session JSONL for the newest `goal_status` (deduped by uuid in `_lastGoalStatusUuid`); on `met` it clears `_goal`, broadcasts `Goal met: ... (reason)`, and writes `set-goal null` back to the wrapper so meta doesn't restore a stale active goal after server restart.
- **Codex**: uses the app-server's **native** goal loop (do NOT simulate). `set-goal` → `thread/goal/set { threadId, objective, status: 'active' }` RPC (stored in Codex SQLite; app-server auto-continues via `MaybeContinueIfIdle` after each turn with developer messages). **`status: 'active'` is REQUIRED**: thread/goal/set is a partial update — omitting status KEEPS the current one, and `continue_if_idle` only fires for Active goals, so re-setting a `usageLimited`/`paused` goal without status silently does nothing (the original Continue Goal bug). There is NO automatic recovery from `usageLimited` — only an explicit set with status active (or the model's own goal tool) reactivates it. Wrapper queries `thread/goal/get` on startup (after `startThread`) and after each `turn/completed` to sync authoritative state — fields are **camelCase**: `objective`, `status` (active/paused/blocked/usageLimited/budgetLimited/complete), `timeUsedSeconds`, `tokensUsed`. `thread/goal/updated`/`thread/goal/cleared` notifications also update meta. Resuming a thread with an active goal auto-continues (Codex design — `emit_resume_goal_snapshot_and_continue`). `thread/goal/clear` removes it.
- **Status bar indicator**: ALWAYS rendered — dim 🎯 when no goal (click → set-a-goal popup with condition input + "Resume previous"); active goal shows 🎯 + status icon (▶ active / ⏸ paused / ⛔ blocked / ✓ complete / ⏳ usageLimited / 🪙 budgetLimited) + elapsed + truncated objective (click → popup with full text, Continue when not active, Clear). Setting `/goal B` while A is active REPLACES it on both backends (Claude: swaps the Stop-hook condition; Codex: `thread/goal/set` updates and steers a running turn with an objective-updated prompt); the WebUI saves the replaced goal to `_prevGoal` for `/goal resume`. Codex resume: the wrapper emits `goal_updated` immediately after its startup `thread/goal/get` — without it the status bar stayed empty for the whole first auto-continued turn.

**System notifications**: Messages containing `<task-notification>`, `<system-reminder>`, and similar tags are detected and rendered as collapsible dim notification cards instead of regular user messages.

**Streaming/Activity Indicator**: Fixed position above the input bar. Shows current activity from live `msg` ops: "thinking..."/"running ToolName"/"responding". Streaming state is tracked by `chat-wrapper.js` in wrapper metadata (`meta.streaming`) — server reads it on attach and sends `isStreaming` in the response. No client-side inference.

**Role Indicators**: `chat.roleIndicator` setting with 4 modes: `border` (default), `background`, `icon`, `label`. Border mode uses `gap:0` between messages with left margin on role switches for continuous colored bars. Background mode tints the message background by role. Icon mode shows role avatars. Label mode shows "You"/"Claude" text labels.

**Chat Font Size**: Follows global A-/A+ font size setting via CSS `zoom` on the message list container.

**View Manager**: Sliding window `[_windowStart, _windowEnd)` over server message list. `jumpToIndex(idx)` replaces window. `jumpToBottom()` loads last 50. `_extendTop()` on scroll-up. Server-side search returns indices, client jumps via `jumpToIndex`. Pagination gated by `_canPaginate` (true for normal and view-only sessions, false for subagent viewers).

**Pin-to-bottom**: Uses iterative scroll convergence (10 rAF frames) instead of single `scrollTop` assignment, for compatibility with `content-visibility: auto` CSS optimization which can cause layout shifts during scroll. Wheel listener at `scrollTop=0` detects upward scroll intent when scroll events stop firing. Auto-fills viewport if content shorter than container.

**View-only mode**: Stopped sessions can be opened as read-only via "📋 View History" button (no `claude --resume`). Server loads JSONL via `viewOnly:true` attach. Also triggered on session exit/terminate — `_setReadOnly()` hides input area, window stays open for reading. View-only sessions use `view-{claudeSessionId}` as virtual session ID, support full scroll-up pagination.

**Highlight Layer**: CSS Custom Highlight API (`CSS.highlights`) — non-destructive rendering layer for search highlighting. `_applyHighlightLayer()` creates Range objects, re-applied on view changes.

**Status Bar**: Model badge (read-only), permission mode (clickable dropdown to change mid-session), background task count (clickable for task detail popup), context % with conic-gradient pie chart (from `assistant.message.usage` per-turn data, NOT cumulative `result.modelUsage`), cache hit ratio, cost with color tiers. ALL of it is server-derived (`chatStatus` in the attach payload) and must survive refresh/restart: the usage scan looks at the newest **2000** records of the merged JSONL+buffer history (200 was too shallow — hundreds of surviving stdout-only system records at the merge tail pushed every assistant usage record out of the window and the context pie vanished on refresh); `_effort` is persisted in session meta like `_permissionMode` (create/resume + every set-effort) since the CLI never reports effort back ($<1 green, $1-5 orange, $>5 red). Persisted via `chatStatus` on attach. Codex extras: reasoning effort shown next to the model (from turn_context), sandbox policy in the permission tooltip, cumulative session token usage (in/cached/out/reasoning) in the context-pie tooltip (from thread/tokenUsage/updated totals).

**Session management**: `mode` field on session object. Stored in session metadata + wrapper metadata. `/api/active` and WebSocket `active-sessions` include mode. Sidebar shows badge for chat sessions. Default mode controlled by `session.defaultMode` setting (default: `chat`). All `createSession` paths respect this setting. Resume: split button toggles Terminal/Chat mode per session, persisted in user state.

**Hook detail in history (2.77.0; noise-filtered 2.79.1; injected context visible 2.80.0)**: the INJECTED context rides its own attachment type `hook_additional_context` ({content:[strings]}, no hookName — missing this type was why '注入的context看不到') → renders as '✓ Hook context: <first-tag>' with the full payload expandable (NEVER truncated since 2.80.1 — the old 20000/600-char slices are gone; the pre starts chat-pre-wrapped, picked up by the STANDARD addWrapToggles toolbar (Wrap/Copy) plus an Editor button in the summary row that opens the full text in a temp editor); content-level dedup (outHead, first 200 chars) collapses it against the same hook's stdout copy. Settings (2.80.0): `chat.showHookCards` (client-side body-class CSS toggle `hide-hook-cards`, instant both directions) + `chat.hideEmptyHooks` (normalizer-level via `MessageManager.getSetting` server injection; applies to newly normalized history). Original entry: JSONL `attachment` records of type hook_success/hook_failure/hook_system_message render as expandable ✓/✗ Hook cards — previously dropped, so history showed only the bare stop_hook_summary; that summary names the first 3 hooks by SHORT name (first script filename extracted from the command — hookInfos often has no name field and the raw command can be a ~1KB embedded shell script, which 2.76.0 dumped inline; full commands live behind the card's expandable body, 2.79.2). NOISE RULES (2.79.1, user report — PostToolUse flooded the chat with blank cards): a SUCCESSFUL hook renders only when it produced real content — the protocol-ack JSON ({continue, suppressOutput, …}) is unwrapped to hookSpecificOutput.additionalContext (or decision/reason) and an empty result skips the card entirely; stderr counts only for FAILED hooks (successful plugins spew ExperimentalWarnings there). Live hook_response + replayed attachment double-render is collapsed by a name+5s dedup window (`_lastHookCard`, registered only when a card is actually created).

**JSONL history**: On chat attach, server normalizes all messages via MessageManager (`convertHistory`) and sends last 50 normalized messages + totalCount. Paginated API: `GET /api/session-messages?claudeSessionId=...&cwd=...&offset=&limit=&search=&turnmap=1`. All responses return normalized messages (tool calls merged, stable IDs).

**Virtual scroll**: Sliding DOM window keeps max ~150 rendered messages. `_extendTop()` loads older messages and trims bottom (`_trimBottom`). `_extendBottom()` loads newer messages when scrolling back down and trims top (`_trimTop`) with scroll position preservation. Live messages while viewing history are deferred (only `_total` incremented, scroll button shows badge count). Position indicator shows `120–170 / 3000` when not pinned to bottom.

**Scroll minimap**: Semantic scrollbar on right side of message list showing conversation structure. User message markers (thin blue lines) and compact/compaction markers (wide red lines). Drag to jump via `jumpToIndex`. Floating label follows cursor showing time + user message preview (first ~10 chars, word-boundary truncated). Turn data from `MessageManager.turnMap()` sent in attach payload or fetched via `?turnmap=1` API. Minimap positioned absolute in container, bounds synced to message list via ResizeObserver. Native scrollbar hidden when minimap active.

**WebSocket reconnect**: On reconnect, all active sessions re-attach automatically.
